2 On three sides of the castle lay a lovely garden with masses of gay , sweet flowers , and velvet lawns all cool and shady , which pleased the eye of the princess .
3 The fruit trees were hung with golden and rosy apples , and nightingales sang in every bush , as the gnome and the princess wandered in the leafy alleys , sometimes gazing at the moon , sometimes pausing to gather the rarest flowers for her adornment .
4 And all the time he was thinking to himself that never , during the hundreds of years he had lived , had he seen so charming a maiden .
5 But the princess felt no such happiness ; in spite of all the magic delights around her she was sad , though she tried to seem content for fear of displeasing the gnome .
6 However , he soon perceived her melancholy , and in a thousand ways strove to dispel the cloud , but in vain .
7 At last he said to himself : ` Men are sociable creatures , like bees or ants .
8 Doubtless this lovely mortal is pining for company .
9 Who is there I can find for her to talk to ? '
10 Thereupon he hastened into the nearest filed and dug up a dozen or so of different roots -- carrots , turnips , and radishes -- and laying them carefully in an elegant basket brought them to the princess , who sat pensive in the shade of the rose-bower .
11 ` Loveliest daughter of earth , ' said the gnome , ` banish all sorrow ; no more shall you be lonely in my dwelling .
12 In this basket is all you need to make this spot delightful to you .
13 Take this little many-coloured wand , and with a touch give to each root the form you desire to see . '
14 With this he left her , and the princess , without an instant 's delay , opened the basket , and touching a turnip , cried eagerly : ` Brunhilda , my dear Brunhilda !
15 come to me quickly ! '
16 And sure enough there was Brunhilda , joyfully hugging and kissing her beloved princess , and chattering as gaily as in the old days .

19 There they found so much to amuse them that the hours passed like minutes .
20 Veils , girdles , and necklaces were tried on and admired , the imitation Brunhilda knew so well how to behave herself , and showed so much taste that nobody would ever have suspected that she was nothing but a turnip after all .

1 On three sides of the castle lay a lovely garden with masses of gay , sweet flowers , and velvet lawns all cool and shady , which pleased the eye of the princess .
2 The fruit trees were hung with golden and rosy apples , and nightingales sang in every bush , as the gnome and the princess wandered in the leafy alleys , sometimes gazing at the moon , sometimes pausing to gather the rarest flowers for her adornment .
3 And all the time he was thinking to himself that never , during the hundreds of years he had lived , had he seen so charming a maiden .
4 But the princess felt no such happiness ; in spite of all the magic delights around her she was sad , though she tried to seem content for fear of displeasing the gnome .
5 However , he soon perceived her melancholy , and in a thousand ways strove to dispel the cloud , but in vain .
6 At last he said to himself : ` Men are sociable creatures , like bees or ants .
7 Doubtless this lovely mortal is pining for company .
8 Who is there I can find for her to talk to ? '
9 Thereupon he hastened into the nearest filed and dug up a dozen or so of different roots -- carrots , turnips , and radishes -- and laying them carefully in an elegant basket brought them to the princess , who sat pensive in the shade of the rose-bower .
10 ` Loveliest daughter of earth , ' said the gnome , ` banish all sorrow ; no more shall you be lonely in my dwelling .
11 In this basket is all you need to make this spot delightful to you .
12 Take this little many-coloured wand , and with a touch give to each root the form you desire to see . '
13 With this he left her , and the princess , without an instant 's delay , opened the basket , and touching a turnip , cried eagerly : ` Brunhilda , my dear Brunhilda !
14 come to me quickly ! '
15 And sure enough there was Brunhilda , joyfully hugging and kissing her beloved princess , and chattering as gaily as in the old days .
16 This sudden appearance was so delightful that the princess could hardly believe her own eyes , and was quite beside herself with the joy of having her dear playfellow with her once more .
17 Hand in hand they wandered about the enchanted garden , and gathered the golden apples from the trees , and when they were tired of this amusement the princess led her friend through all the wonderful rooms of the palace , until at last they came to the one in which were kept all the marvellous dresses and ornaments the gnome had given to his hoped-for bride .
18 There they found so much to amuse them that the hours passed like minutes .
19 Veils , girdles , and necklaces were tried on and admired , the imitation Brunhilda knew so well how to behave herself , and showed so much taste that nobody would ever have suspected that she was nothing but a turnip after all .
20 The gnome , who had secretly been keeping an eye upon them , was very pleased with himself for having so well understood the heart of a woman ; and the princess seemed to him even more charming than before .

1 And all the time he was thinking to himself that never , during the hundreds of years he had lived , had he seen so charming a maiden .
2 But the princess felt no such happiness ; in spite of all the magic delights around her she was sad , though she tried to seem content for fear of displeasing the gnome .
3 However , he soon perceived her melancholy , and in a thousand ways strove to dispel the cloud , but in vain .
4 At last he said to himself : ` Men are sociable creatures , like bees or ants .
5 Doubtless this lovely mortal is pining for company .
6 Who is there I can find for her to talk to ? '
7 Thereupon he hastened into the nearest filed and dug up a dozen or so of different roots -- carrots , turnips , and radishes -- and laying them carefully in an elegant basket brought them to the princess , who sat pensive in the shade of the rose-bower .
8 ` Loveliest daughter of earth , ' said the gnome , ` banish all sorrow ; no more shall you be lonely in my dwelling .
9 In this basket is all you need to make this spot delightful to you .
10 Take this little many-coloured wand , and with a touch give to each root the form you desire to see . '
11 With this he left her , and the princess , without an instant 's delay , opened the basket , and touching a turnip , cried eagerly : ` Brunhilda , my dear Brunhilda !
12 come to me quickly ! '
13 And sure enough there was Brunhilda , joyfully hugging and kissing her beloved princess , and chattering as gaily as in the old days .
14 This sudden appearance was so delightful that the princess could hardly believe her own eyes , and was quite beside herself with the joy of having her dear playfellow with her once more .
15 Hand in hand they wandered about the enchanted garden , and gathered the golden apples from the trees , and when they were tired of this amusement the princess led her friend through all the wonderful rooms of the palace , until at last they came to the one in which were kept all the marvellous dresses and ornaments the gnome had given to his hoped-for bride .
16 There they found so much to amuse them that the hours passed like minutes .
17 Veils , girdles , and necklaces were tried on and admired , the imitation Brunhilda knew so well how to behave herself , and showed so much taste that nobody would ever have suspected that she was nothing but a turnip after all .
18 The gnome , who had secretly been keeping an eye upon them , was very pleased with himself for having so well understood the heart of a woman ; and the princess seemed to him even more charming than before .
19 She did not forget to touch the rest of the roots with her magic wand , and soon had all her maidens about her , and even , as she had two tiny radishes to spare , her favourite cat , and her little dog whose name was Beni .
20 And now all went cheerfully in the castle .

1 And all the time he was thinking to himself that never , during the hundreds of years he had lived , had he seen so charming a maiden .
2 But the princess felt no such happiness ; in spite of all the magic delights around her she was sad , though she tried to seem content for fear of displeasing the gnome .
3 However , he soon perceived her melancholy , and in a thousand ways strove to dispel the cloud , but in vain .
4 At last he said to himself : ` Men are sociable creatures , like bees or ants .
5 Doubtless this lovely mortal is pining for company .
6 Who is there I can find for her to talk to ? '
7 Thereupon he hastened into the nearest filed and dug up a dozen or so of different roots -- carrots , turnips , and radishes -- and laying them carefully in an elegant basket brought them to the princess , who sat pensive in the shade of the rose-bower .
8 ` Loveliest daughter of earth , ' said the gnome , ` banish all sorrow ; no more shall you be lonely in my dwelling .
9 In this basket is all you need to make this spot delightful to you .
10 Take this little many-coloured wand , and with a touch give to each root the form you desire to see . '
11 With this he left her , and the princess , without an instant 's delay , opened the basket , and touching a turnip , cried eagerly : ` Brunhilda , my dear Brunhilda !
12 come to me quickly ! '
13 And sure enough there was Brunhilda , joyfully hugging and kissing her beloved princess , and chattering as gaily as in the old days .
14 This sudden appearance was so delightful that the princess could hardly believe her own eyes , and was quite beside herself with the joy of having her dear playfellow with her once more .
15 Hand in hand they wandered about the enchanted garden , and gathered the golden apples from the trees , and when they were tired of this amusement the princess led her friend through all the wonderful rooms of the palace , until at last they came to the one in which were kept all the marvellous dresses and ornaments the gnome had given to his hoped-for bride .
16 There they found so much to amuse them that the hours passed like minutes .
17 Veils , girdles , and necklaces were tried on and admired , the imitation Brunhilda knew so well how to behave herself , and showed so much taste that nobody would ever have suspected that she was nothing but a turnip after all .
18 The gnome , who had secretly been keeping an eye upon them , was very pleased with himself for having so well understood the heart of a woman ; and the princess seemed to him even more charming than before .
19 She did not forget to touch the rest of the roots with her magic wand , and soon had all her maidens about her , and even , as she had two tiny radishes to spare , her favourite cat , and her little dog whose name was Beni .
20 And now all went cheerfully in the castle .
21 The princess gave to each of the XXXXX her task , and never was mistress better served .	maidens		basket|company|hand|happiness|maidens|necklaces|palace|rest|time|ways

1 However , he soon perceived her melancholy , and in a thousand ways strove to dispel the cloud , but in vain .
2 At last he said to himself : ` Men are sociable creatures , like bees or ants .
3 Doubtless this lovely mortal is pining for company .
4 Who is there I can find for her to talk to ? '
5 Thereupon he hastened into the nearest filed and dug up a dozen or so of different roots -- carrots , turnips , and radishes -- and laying them carefully in an elegant basket brought them to the princess , who sat pensive in the shade of the rose-bower .
6 ` Loveliest daughter of earth , ' said the gnome , ` banish all sorrow ; no more shall you be lonely in my dwelling .
7 In this basket is all you need to make this spot delightful to you .
8 Take this little many-coloured wand , and with a touch give to each root the form you desire to see . '
9 With this he left her , and the princess , without an instant 's delay , opened the basket , and touching a turnip , cried eagerly : ` Brunhilda , my dear Brunhilda !
10 come to me quickly ! '
11 And sure enough there was Brunhilda , joyfully hugging and kissing her beloved princess , and chattering as gaily as in the old days .
12 This sudden appearance was so delightful that the princess could hardly believe her own eyes , and was quite beside herself with the joy of having her dear playfellow with her once more .
13 Hand in hand they wandered about the enchanted garden , and gathered the golden apples from the trees , and when they were tired of this amusement the princess led her friend through all the wonderful rooms of the palace , until at last they came to the one in which were kept all the marvellous dresses and ornaments the gnome had given to his hoped-for bride .
14 There they found so much to amuse them that the hours passed like minutes .
15 Veils , girdles , and necklaces were tried on and admired , the imitation Brunhilda knew so well how to behave herself , and showed so much taste that nobody would ever have suspected that she was nothing but a turnip after all .
16 The gnome , who had secretly been keeping an eye upon them , was very pleased with himself for having so well understood the heart of a woman ; and the princess seemed to him even more charming than before .
17 She did not forget to touch the rest of the roots with her magic wand , and soon had all her maidens about her , and even , as she had two tiny radishes to spare , her favourite cat , and her little dog whose name was Beni .
18 And now all went cheerfully in the castle .
19 The princess gave to each of the maidens her task , and never was mistress better served .
20 For a whole week she enjoyed the delight of her pleasant company undisturbed .
21 They all sang , they danced , they played from morning to night ; only the XXXXX noticed that day by day the fresh young faces of her maidens grew pale and wan , and the mirror in the great marble hall showed her that she alone still kept her rosy bloom , while Brunhilda and the rest faded visibly .	princess		amusement|dog|dresses|hand|instant|name|palace|princess|turnips|ways

13 Hand in hand they wandered about the enchanted garden , and gathered the golden apples from the trees , and when they were tired of this amusement the princess led her friend through all the wonderful rooms of the palace , until at last they came to the one in which were kept all the marvellous dresses and ornaments the gnome had given to his hoped-for bride .
14 There they found so much to amuse them that the hours passed like minutes .
15 Veils , girdles , and necklaces were tried on and admired , the imitation Brunhilda knew so well how to behave herself , and showed so much taste that nobody would ever have suspected that she was nothing but a turnip after all .
16 The gnome , who had secretly been keeping an eye upon them , was very pleased with himself for having so well understood the heart of a woman ; and the princess seemed to him even more charming than before .
17 She did not forget to touch the rest of the roots with her magic wand , and soon had all her maidens about her , and even , as she had two tiny radishes to spare , her favourite cat , and her little dog whose name was Beni .
18 And now all went cheerfully in the castle .
19 The princess gave to each of the maidens her task , and never was mistress better served .
20 For a whole week she enjoyed the delight of her pleasant company undisturbed .
21 They all sang , they danced , they played from morning to night ; only the princess noticed that day by day the fresh young faces of her XXXXX grew pale and wan , and the mirror in the great marble hall showed her that she alone still kept her rosy bloom , while Brunhilda and the rest faded visibly .	maidens		Men|Veils|bride|delay|dozen|form|friend|garden|maidens|rooms

1 At last he said to himself : ` Men are sociable creatures , like bees or ants .
2 Doubtless this lovely mortal is pining for company .
3 Who is there I can find for her to talk to ? '
4 Thereupon he hastened into the nearest filed and dug up a dozen or so of different roots -- carrots , turnips , and radishes -- and laying them carefully in an elegant basket brought them to the princess , who sat pensive in the shade of the rose-bower .
5 ` Loveliest daughter of earth , ' said the gnome , ` banish all sorrow ; no more shall you be lonely in my dwelling .
6 In this basket is all you need to make this spot delightful to you .
7 Take this little many-coloured wand , and with a touch give to each root the form you desire to see . '
8 With this he left her , and the princess , without an instant 's delay , opened the basket , and touching a turnip , cried eagerly : ` Brunhilda , my dear Brunhilda !
9 come to me quickly ! '
10 And sure enough there was Brunhilda , joyfully hugging and kissing her beloved princess , and chattering as gaily as in the old days .
11 This sudden appearance was so delightful that the princess could hardly believe her own eyes , and was quite beside herself with the joy of having her dear playfellow with her once more .
12 Hand in hand they wandered about the enchanted garden , and gathered the golden apples from the trees , and when they were tired of this amusement the princess led her friend through all the wonderful rooms of the palace , until at last they came to the one in which were kept all the marvellous dresses and ornaments the gnome had given to his hoped-for bride .
13 There they found so much to amuse them that the hours passed like minutes .
14 Veils , girdles , and necklaces were tried on and admired , the imitation Brunhilda knew so well how to behave herself , and showed so much taste that nobody would ever have suspected that she was nothing but a turnip after all .
15 The gnome , who had secretly been keeping an eye upon them , was very pleased with himself for having so well understood the heart of a woman ; and the princess seemed to him even more charming than before .

18 The princess gave to each of the maidens her task , and never was mistress better served .

18 ` Malicious Sprite , ' she cried , ` why do you begrudge me my playmates -- the greatest delight of my lonely hours ?
19 Is n't this solitary life in such a desert bad enough without your turning the castle into a hospital for the aged ?
20 Give my maidens back their youth and health this very minute , or I will never love you ! '
21 ` Sweetest and fairest of damsels , ' cried the XXXXX , ` do not be angry ; everything that is in my power I will do -- but do not ask the impossible .	gnome		cat|delay|faces|garden|gnome|head|heart|palace|woman|youth

1 With this he left her , and the princess , without an instant 's delay , opened the basket , and touching a turnip , cried eagerly : ` Brunhilda , my dear Brunhilda !
2 come to me quickly ! '
3 And sure enough there was Brunhilda , joyfully hugging and kissing her beloved princess , and chattering as gaily as in the old days .
4 This sudden appearance was so delightful that the princess could hardly believe her own eyes , and was quite beside herself with the joy of having her dear playfellow with her once more .
5 Hand in hand they wandered about the enchanted garden , and gathered the golden apples from the trees , and when they were tired of this amusement the princess led her friend through all the wonderful rooms of the palace , until at last they came to the one in which were kept all the marvellous dresses and ornaments the gnome had given to his hoped-for bride .
6 There they found so much to amuse them that the hours passed like minutes .
7 Veils , girdles , and necklaces were tried on and admired , the imitation Brunhilda knew so well how to behave herself , and showed so much taste that nobody would ever have suspected that she was nothing but a turnip after all .
8 The gnome , who had secretly been keeping an eye upon them , was very pleased with himself for having so well understood the heart of a woman ; and the princess seemed to him even more charming than before .
9 She did not forget to touch the rest of the roots with her magic wand , and soon had all her maidens about her , and even , as she had two tiny radishes to spare , her favourite cat , and her little dog whose name was Beni .
10 And now all went cheerfully in the castle .
11 The princess gave to each of the maidens her task , and never was mistress better served .
12 For a whole week she enjoyed the delight of her pleasant company undisturbed .
13 They all sang , they danced , they played from morning to night ; only the princess noticed that day by day the fresh young faces of her maidens grew pale and wan , and the mirror in the great marble hall showed her that she alone still kept her rosy bloom , while Brunhilda and the rest faded visibly .
14 They assured her that all was well with them ; but , nevertheless , they continued to waste away , and day by day it became harder to them to take part in the games of the princess , till at last , one fine morning , when the princess started from bed and hastened out to join her gay playfellows , she shuddered and started back at the sight of a group of shrivelled crones , with bent backs and trembling limbs , who supported their tottering steps with staves and crutches , and coughed dismally .
15 A little nearer to the hearth lay the once frolicsome Beni , with all four feet stretched stiffly out , while the sleek cat seemed too weak to raise his head from his velvet cushion .
16 The horrified princess fled to the door to escape from the sight of this mournful company , and called loudly for the gnome , who appeared at once , humbly anxious to do her bidding .
17 ` Malicious Sprite , ' she cried , ` why do you begrudge me my playmates -- the greatest delight of my lonely hours ?
18 Is n't this solitary life in such a desert bad enough without your turning the castle into a hospital for the aged ?
19 Give my maidens back their youth and health this very minute , or I will never love you ! '
20 ` Sweetest and fairest of damsels , ' cried the gnome , ` do not be angry ; everything that is in my power I will do -- but do not ask the impossible .
21 So long as the sap was fresh in the XXXXX the magic staff could keep them in the forms you desired , but as the sap dried up they withered away .	roots		Sprite|Veils|castle|desert|faces|friend|health|palace|roots|youth

21 Up and down the XXXXX she searched , spying into every corner , but not a sign of it was to be found .	garden		Veils|basket|cat|games|garden|hearth|playmates|power|woman|women

1 And now all went cheerfully in the castle .
2 The princess gave to each of the maidens her task , and never was mistress better served .
3 For a whole week she enjoyed the delight of her pleasant company undisturbed .
4 They all sang , they danced , they played from morning to night ; only the princess noticed that day by day the fresh young faces of her maidens grew pale and wan , and the mirror in the great marble hall showed her that she alone still kept her rosy bloom , while Brunhilda and the rest faded visibly .
5 They assured her that all was well with them ; but , nevertheless , they continued to waste away , and day by day it became harder to them to take part in the games of the princess , till at last , one fine morning , when the princess started from bed and hastened out to join her gay playfellows , she shuddered and started back at the sight of a group of shrivelled crones , with bent backs and trembling limbs , who supported their tottering steps with staves and crutches , and coughed dismally .
6 A little nearer to the hearth lay the once frolicsome Beni , with all four feet stretched stiffly out , while the sleek cat seemed too weak to raise his head from his velvet cushion .
7 The horrified princess fled to the door to escape from the sight of this mournful company , and called loudly for the gnome , who appeared at once , humbly anxious to do her bidding .
8 ` Malicious Sprite , ' she cried , ` why do you begrudge me my playmates -- the greatest delight of my lonely hours ?
9 Is n't this solitary life in such a desert bad enough without your turning the castle into a hospital for the aged ?
10 Give my maidens back their youth and health this very minute , or I will never love you ! '
11 ` Sweetest and fairest of damsels , ' cried the gnome , ` do not be angry ; everything that is in my power I will do -- but do not ask the impossible .
12 So long as the sap was fresh in the roots the magic staff could keep them in the forms you desired , but as the sap dried up they withered away .
13 But never trouble yourself about that , dearest one , a basket of fresh turnips will soon set matters right , and you can speedily call up again every form you wish to see .
14 The great green patch in the garden will prove you with a more lively company . '
15 So saying the gnome took himself off .
16 And the princess with her magic wand touched the wrinkled old women , and left them the withered roots they really were , to be thrown upon the rubbish heap ; and with light feet skipped off across to the meadow to take possession of the freshly filled basket .
17 But to her surprise she could not find it anywhere .
18 Up and down the garden she searched , spying into every corner , but not a sign of it was to be found .
19 By the trellis of grape vines she met the gnome , who was so much embarrassed at the sight of her that she became aware of his confusion while he was still quite a long way off .
20 ` You are trying to tease me , ' she cried , as soon as she saw him .
21 ` Where have you hidden the XXXXX ?	basket		basket|castle|delight|gnome|head|heap|life|maidens|trouble|wan

14 Almost before the gnome had finished , the disappointed princess turned away , and marched off to her own apartments , without deigning to answer him .
15 The gnome , however , set off above ground as speedily as possible , and disguising himself as a farmer , bought an ass in the nearest market-town , and brought it back loaded with sacks of turnip , carrot , and radish seed .
16 With this he sowed a great field , and sent a vast army of his goblins to watch and tend it , and to bring up the fiery rivers from the heart of the earth near enough to warm and encourage the sprouting seeds .
17 Thus fostered they grew and flourished marvellously , and promised a goodly crop .
18 The princess wandered about the field day by day , no other plants or fruits in all her wonderful garden pleased her as much as these roots ; but still her eyes were full of discontent .
19 And , best of all , she loved to while away the hours in a shady fir-wood , seated upon the bank of a little stream , into which she would cast the flowers she had gathered and watch them float away .
20 The gnome tried hard by every means in his power to please the princess and win her love , but little did he guess the real reason of his lack of success .
21 He imagined that she was too young and inexperienced to care for him ; but that was a mistake , for the truth was that another image already filled her XXXXX .	heart		ass|bank|flowers|heart|means|patience|puppets|reason|seeds|women

1 So saying the gnome took himself off .
2 And the princess with her magic wand touched the wrinkled old women , and left them the withered roots they really were , to be thrown upon the rubbish heap ; and with light feet skipped off across to the meadow to take possession of the freshly filled basket .
3 But to her surprise she could not find it anywhere .
4 Up and down the garden she searched , spying into every corner , but not a sign of it was to be found .
5 By the trellis of grape vines she met the gnome , who was so much embarrassed at the sight of her that she became aware of his confusion while he was still quite a long way off .
6 ` You are trying to tease me , ' she cried , as soon as she saw him .
7 ` Where have you hidden the basket ?
8 I have been looking for it at least an hour . '

14 Meanwhile , the maiden , in her gorgeous prison , sighed in secret over her grief , not wishing to arouse the gnome 's suspicions .
15 In her own mind she was wondering if by any means she might escape from her captivity , and at last she hit upon a plan .
16 By this time spring once more reigned in the valley , and the gnome sent the fires back to their places in the deeps of the earth , for the roots which they had kept warm through all the cruel winter hand now come to their full size .
17 Day by day the princess pulled up some of them , and made experiments with them , conjuring up now this longed-for person , and now that , just for the pleasure of seeing them as they appeared ; but she really had another purpose in view .
18 One day she changed a tiny turnip into a bee , and sent him off to bring her some news of her lover .
19 ` Fly , dear little bee , towards the east , ' said she , ` to my beloved Ratibor , and softly hum into his ear that I love him only , but that I am a captive in the gnome 's palace under the mountains .
20 Do not forget a single word of my greeting , and bring me back a message from my beloved . '
21 So the XXXXX spread his shining wings and flew away to do as he was bidden ; but before he was out of sight a greedy swallow made a snatch at him , and to the great grief of the princess her messenger was eaten up then and there .	bee		bee|bride|garden|image|lands|mountains|pleasure|puppets|sacks|seed

1 I promised more than I could perform .
2 I have sought all over the land for the roots you desire ; but they are gathered in , and lie drying in musty cellars , and the fields are bare and desolate , for below in the valley winter reigns , only here in your presence spring is held fast , and wherever your foot is set the gay flowers bloom .
3 Have patience for a little , and then without fail you shall have your puppets to play with . '
4 Almost before the gnome had finished , the disappointed princess turned away , and marched off to her own apartments , without deigning to answer him .
5 The gnome , however , set off above ground as speedily as possible , and disguising himself as a farmer , bought an ass in the nearest market-town , and brought it back loaded with sacks of turnip , carrot , and radish seed .
6 With this he sowed a great field , and sent a vast army of his goblins to watch and tend it , and to bring up the fiery rivers from the heart of the earth near enough to warm and encourage the sprouting seeds .
7 Thus fostered they grew and flourished marvellously , and promised a goodly crop .
8 The princess wandered about the field day by day , no other plants or fruits in all her wonderful garden pleased her as much as these roots ; but still her eyes were full of discontent .
9 And , best of all , she loved to while away the hours in a shady fir-wood , seated upon the bank of a little stream , into which she would cast the flowers she had gathered and watch them float away .
10 The gnome tried hard by every means in his power to please the princess and win her love , but little did he guess the real reason of his lack of success .
11 He imagined that she was too young and inexperienced to care for him ; but that was a mistake , for the truth was that another image already filled her heart .
12 The young Prince Ratibor , whose lands joined her father 's , had won the heart of the princess ; and the lovers had been looking forward to the coming of their wedding-day when the bride 's mysterious disappearance took place .
13 The sad news drove Ratibor distracted , and as the days went on , and nothing could be heard of the princess , he forsook his castle and the society of men , and spent his days in the wild forests , roaming about and crying her name aloud to the trees and rocks .
14 Meanwhile , the maiden , in her gorgeous prison , sighed in secret over her grief , not wishing to arouse the gnome 's suspicions .
15 In her own mind she was wondering if by any means she might escape from her captivity , and at last she hit upon a plan .
16 By this time spring once more reigned in the valley , and the gnome sent the fires back to their places in the deeps of the earth , for the roots which they had kept warm through all the cruel winter hand now come to their full size .
17 Day by day the princess pulled up some of them , and made experiments with them , conjuring up now this longed-for person , and now that , just for the pleasure of seeing them as they appeared ; but she really had another purpose in view .
18 One day she changed a tiny turnip into a bee , and sent him off to bring her some news of her lover .
19 ` Fly , dear little bee , towards the east , ' said she , ` to my beloved Ratibor , and softly hum into his ear that I love him only , but that I am a captive in the gnome 's palace under the mountains .
20 Do not forget a single word of my greeting , and bring me back a message from my beloved . '
